b the erection of a newTheatre, felicitous only that, without enlarging the audienceDart of the edifice, it might afford the Publick improved accommodation and feeurily,
tmdat the fame time, prefent an additional ornament to the Metropolis of the Britiih
Umpire. This, their molt anxious with, they flatter themfelves, they have folidly
fleeted, not only within the lhort fpace of ten months lioni the laying of the founda;ions, but under the enormoufly expenfive disadvantage of cireumftanees iingularly
jufavouralile 10 building.—When it is known that no left a funi than one hundred
<nd fifty thoufand pounds has been expended in order to render this Theatre worthy
if Britifh Spectators, and of the Genius of their native Poets :—when, in this undertaking, the inevitable accumulation of, at leaft, aiixfbld rentage is pofitiv el v Rated to
be incurred ;— and when, in addition to thefe preflirig incumbrances, the enereaied

per anrium, chargi-nt the concern with only thefonria«5tually paid for infuranee on
ueh part of the capital as Was hlfurcd; h«t, if the whole of the capital had been
'TWiH-ittTht profit would have been reduced to very little more than five per cent.—
md, for want of this full infurance, the Proprietors being in part their own infurers,
.idhiiin-d a loft, by the late fire for which no componfatiou Iras been nrnlc, to the
itnount of more than,the whole of their profits for the alum- perilul of (ix years.
The rate-of profit likely to be received tjitfutare iroin the new Tin ..tie, dejpending

if the fame J>e ini'ured; and that, upon the fame fuppolitam of infuianee, at the former

The Committee for examining tin- affairs of Caveat Gtrrden Theatre, cor,f; fling iif the
following Gentfciiien:—Alderman Sir 'Charles Price, Jit. MP.—Sir 'Ihourax Plunter, %t.
his Majefiifs Sq/ici/or General—John Siiie/ier, E/q. Recorder of the City ofLondcrr—
«/oh» Whit/nore, Efb. Governorofthe Bank pf England—and John J alius Angerjicin,
Eft/, have author*fed the Proprietors to ptiblifh the following Report in their names.
We do hereby certify that, after a full and attentive examination of the fubject
which we have been delhed to invettignte by the Proprietors of Covent Garden
Theatre for the fatisfaction of the Punlick, in relpect to the rate of profit receive.'
by them from the late Theatre, and likely to be received from the new, that the
following is me reftilt of odr enquiry—
The rate of profit afctually received, upon an average of the laft fix years commencing in IHM, (the period of the prefect co-partnerihip in the Theatre) upon the
capital embarked therein, we have afecrtnined to have.amounted to b'f per cent.
>er annum, charging the concern with only the linn actually paid for infurance ort.
iich part of the capital as was infured; but, if the whole of the capital had been
infured, the profit would have been reduced to very little more than five per cent.—
and, for want of this full infurance, the Proprietors being in part their own infurers,
fuftained a lofs by the late fire for which no compenfation has been made, to the
•amount of more than the whole of their pnifits for the above period of fix years.
The rate of profit likely to be received in future from the new Theatre, depending
in part upon the amount of bills not yet delivered, and of eftimates not fully alcertained, and on the future receipts of the houfe, which are fubject to various contingencies, cannot be afcertained. with the lame degree of certainty ; but, upon the
heft coniideration we have beep able to give to this fubject, after having recourfe to
eveiy fource of information, oral and written, vve are fully fatisfied that the future
profits of the new Theatre, at the propofed advance in the prices of atlniilfion, will
amount to only 3j per cent, per annum upon the capital expended in the 'I heatre,
if the fame be infured; and that, upon the fame fuppolition ofinfurance, at the former
prices of adniiflinn, the Proprietors will, in our judgment, annually fuftain a lols of
nearly three-fourths per cent, per annum on their capital.
CHARLES PRICE. THOMAS PLUMER. JOHN SILVESTER
JOHN WHITMORE. JOHN JULIUS ANGKRSTEIN.

TO T H E FUBLICK.

With the ntmoft concern the Proprietors feel themielves compelled to make this
addrels to the juftice of the Publiek.
In an appeal to the Town at the elofe of lair feafoti, a full and tliftin6t defeription was given of the alterations propoled to be made in the new Theatre.—This
appeal was honoured with the general approbation of a very crowded audience: and
the Proprietors, on the faith of* this approbation, at a heavy additional expenle
{which they could but ill afford) have com pleated thole alterations.
The new Theatre (with much more fpace in the puhiick Bcxes, and general accommodation in every refpefct improved) is now reftored to ti.e fame arrangement
with that of the old Theatre before the Eire :—and the publick certainly will not
defire that the Proprietors, with all their additional heavy incumbrances, fliould be
redu-ed to a more difadvantageous fituation than they flood in before that afflicting
calamity.—There is not one more annua! Bos now, than diere was in the old Theatre,
and lo that number for many years there never was heard the High tell objection.
The Proprietors throw themfelves on the characteriliick juliice and liberality of
Engiiflimen, and in return for the great anxiety, expenfe, and refponAbility which
they have cheerfully encountered in order to contribute on an extenfive fcale to the
Theatrical 1 ntertainments of the Metropolis, they refpectftdly folicit the patronage
and fupport of the Publiek.
